25:T2ff0,<entryFree id="n26607" key="طَرَفَ" type="main">

                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">طَرَفَ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">طَرِفَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">طَرْفٌ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">He looked from the outer angle of the eye:</hi> or [<hi rend="ital">he twinkled with his eye,</hi> i. e.] <hi rend="ital">he put the edge of his eyelid in motion,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in a state of commotion, and looked:</hi> (M, TA:) or <foreign lang="ar">الطَّرْفُ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">the putting the eyelids in motion,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in a state of commotion, in looking:</hi> (Mgh, * TA:) one says, <foreign lang="ar">شَخَصَ بَصَرُهُ فَمَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">يَطْرِفُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">His eye,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">eyes, has,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">have, become fixedly open,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">raised, and he does not put his eyelids in motion,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">does not twinkle with his eye,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">eyes, in looking</hi>]: (TA:) [or] one says, <foreign lang="ar">طَرَفَ البَصَرُ</foreign>, aor. and inf. n. as above, meaning <hi rend="ital">the eye,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">eyes,</hi> [<hi rend="ital">twinkled,</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">became in a state of commotion:</hi> (Msb:) [or] <foreign lang="ar">طَرَفَ بَصَرَهُ</foreign>, (O, K, TA, and so in a copy of the S,) or <foreign lang="ar">بَصَرُهُ</foreign>, (so in one of my copies of the S,) aor. and inf. n. as above, [<hi rend="ital">he winked,</hi> i. e.] <hi rend="ital">he closed one of his eyelids upon the other:</hi> (S, O, K: [see also 4:]) or <foreign lang="ar">طَرَفَ بِعَيْنِهِ</foreign> [in the CK <foreign lang="ar">بعَيْنَيْهِ</foreign>] <hi rend="ital">he put his eyelids in motion,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in a state of commotion:</hi> (K, TA:) and <foreign lang="ar">طُرِفَتْ عَيْنُهُ</foreign>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">تُطْرَفُ</foreign>, inf. n. as above, <hi rend="ital">his eyelids were put in motion</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in a state of commotion, by looking.</hi> (As, TA.) [Another meaning of <foreign lang="ar">طَرَفَ بَصَرَهُ</foreign>, and another of <foreign lang="ar">طُرِفَتْ</foreign> said of the eye, will be found below.] <foreign lang="ar">عَيْنٌ تَطْرِفُ</foreign>, signifying <hi rend="ital">An eye that</hi> [<hi rend="ital">twinkles,</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">puts the eyelid in motion,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in a state of commotion, with looking,</hi> is used for <foreign lang="ar">ذُو عَيْنٍ تَطْرِفُ</foreign>, meaning <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">a living being.</hi> (Mgh.) <foreign lang="ar">مَا بَقِيَتْ مِنْهُمْ عَيْنٌ تَطْرِفُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">There remained not of them</hi> one having <hi rend="ital">an eye twinkling</hi>] means <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">they died,</hi> (O, K, TA,) or (O, in the K erroneously “ and, ” TA) <hi rend="ital">they were slain.</hi> (O, K, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Also <hi rend="ital">He looked:</hi> for] <foreign lang="ar">الطَّرْفُ</foreign> is used as meaning <hi rend="ital">the act of looking</hi> (Er-Rághib, Msb, TA) because the putting in motion of the eyelid constantly attends that act: (Er-Rághib, TA:) and <foreign lang="ar">طَرَفْتُهُ</foreign>, inf. n. as above, signifies <hi rend="ital">I saw,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">I looked at</hi> or <hi rend="ital">towards, him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">أَبْصَرْتُهُ</foreign>. (Ham p. 111.) It is said in the Kur [xiv. 44] <foreign lang="ar">لَا يَرْتَدُّ إِلَيْهِمْ طَرْفُهُمْ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Their look shall not revert to them;</hi> i. e., <hi rend="ital">shall not be withdrawn by them</hi> from that upon which they shall look]. (S, O.) And in the same [xxvii. 40], <foreign lang="ar">أَنَا آتِيكَ بِهِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَرْتَدٌ إِلَيْكَ طَرْفُكَ</foreign>, [meaning, in like manner, <hi rend="ital">I will bring it to thee before thy look</hi> at a thing <hi rend="ital">shall revert to thee,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">be withdrawn by thee</hi> therefrom: or,] accord. to Fr, meaning <hi rend="ital">before a thing shall be brought to thee</hi> 
                  <pb n="1842"/> 
                  <hi rend="ital">from the extent of thy vision:</hi> or, as some say, <hi rend="ital">in the space in which thou shalt open thine eye and then close it:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in the space in which one shall reach the extent of thy vision.</hi> (O.) And one says, <foreign lang="ar">نَظَرَ فُلَانٌ بِطَرْفٍ خَفِىٍّ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Such a one looked with a furtive glance</hi>], meaning, <hi rend="ital">contracted his eyelids over the main portion of his eye and looked with the rest of it,</hi> by reason of shyness or fear. (Har p. 565.) And <foreign lang="ar">تَطْرِفُ الرِّجَالَ</foreign> [app. meaning <hi rend="ital">She looks at the men</hi>] is said of a woman who does not keep constantly to one. (TA. [See <foreign lang="ar">مَطْرُوفَةٌ</foreign>.]) And <foreign lang="ar">تَطْرِفُ الرِّيَاضَ رَوْضَةً بَعْدَ رَوْضَةٍ</foreign> [app. meaning <hi rend="ital">She looks at the meadows, meadow after meadow,</hi> to pasture upon them in succession,] is said of a she-camel such as is termed <foreign lang="ar">طَرِفَةٌ</foreign> [q. v.]. (As, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">طَرَفْتُ عَيْنَهُ</foreign>, (S, O, Msb, in the K <foreign lang="ar">طَرَفَ عَيْنَهُ</foreign>,) aor. and inf. n. as above, (Msb, TA,) <hi rend="ital">I</hi> (S, O, Msb) <hi rend="ital">hit, struck, smote,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">hurt, his eye with a thing,</hi> (S, O, Msb, K, [in the CK <foreign lang="ar">شَىْءٌ</foreign> is put for <foreign lang="ar">بِشَىْءٍ</foreign>,]) such as a garment or some other thing, (TA,) <hi rend="ital">so that it shed tears:</hi> and one says of the eye, <foreign lang="ar">طُرِفَتْ</foreign>. (S, O, K. [See another explanation of the latter in the first sentence.]) Ziyád, in reciting a <foreign lang="ar">خُطْبَة</foreign>, said, <foreign lang="ar">قَدْ طَرَفَتْ أَعْيُنَكُمُ الدُّنْيَا وَسَدَّتْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مَسَامِعَكُمُ الشَّهَوَاتُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The good of the present world hath smitten your eyes, and appetences have stopped your ears</hi>]. (O.) And one says <foreign lang="ar">طَرَفَهُ</foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n26607-1" target="طرّفهُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n26608"/></foreign> meaning <hi rend="ital">He,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, struck, smote,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">hurt, his eye.</hi> (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">طَرَفَهَا الحُزْنُ وَالبُكَآءُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Grief and weeping hurt it</hi> (the eye), <hi rend="ital">so that it shed tears.</hi> (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">طَرَفَهَا حُبُّ الرِّجَالِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The love of the men smote her eye, so that she raised her eyes and looked at every one that looked at her;</hi> as though a <foreign lang="ar">طَرْفَة</foreign> [or red spot of blood], or a stick or the like, hurt her eye. (Az, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">الطَّرْفُ</foreign> signifies also <hi rend="ital">The slapping with the hand</hi> (K, TA) <hi rend="ital">upon the extremity of the eye.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  Then it became applied to signify <hi rend="ital">The striking upon the head.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">طَرَفَهُ عَنْهُ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">He turned him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, away,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">back, from him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it.</hi> (S, O, K.) Hence the saying of a poet, (S, O, TA,) 'Amr Ibn-Abee-Rabee'ah, (TA,) or a young woman of the Ansár, (O,) <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّكَ وَٱللّٰهِ لَذُو مَلَّةٍ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>

                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">طَرْفٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> The <hi rend="ital">eye;</hi> a word having no pl. in this sense because it is originally an inf. n., (S, O, K,) therefore it may denote a sing. and may also denote a pl. number [i. e. may signify also <hi rend="ital">eyes</hi>]: (S, O, Msb:) or, (K,) as Ibn-'Abbád says, (O,) it is a coll. n. signifying the <foreign lang="ar">بَصَر</foreign> [which has the sing. and the pl. meanings mentioned above, as well as the meaning of the <hi rend="ital">sense of sight</hi>], and is not dualized nor pluralized: or, as some say, it has for pl. <foreign lang="ar">أَطْرَافٌ</foreign>: (O, K:) but this is refuted by the occurrence of <foreign lang="ar">طَرْف</foreign> in a pl. sense in the Kur xxxvii. 47 and xxxviii. 52 and lv. 56: (O:) and though <foreign lang="ar">الأَطْرَاف</foreign> is said to occur as its pl. in a trad. of Umm-Selemeh, this is a mistake for <foreign lang="ar">الإِطْرَاق</foreign>: (Z, O:) it is said, however, that its being originally an inf. n. is not a reason for its not being allowable to pluralize it when it has become a subst., and especially when it is not meant to convey the signification of an epithet: (MF:) [but it may be regarded as an epithet; meaning <hi rend="ital">seer,</hi> and, being originally an inf. n., <hi rend="ital">seers</hi> also; and this is the more probable because]

                  </form> A <hi rend="ital">generous</hi> horse: (As, S, O, K:) or, accord. to Er-Rághib, one <hi rend="ital">that is looked at</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">يُطْرَفُ</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">because of his beauty;</hi> so that it is originally <foreign lang="ar">مَطْرُوفٌ</foreign>, i. e. <foreign lang="ar">مَنْظُورٌ</foreign>; like <foreign lang="ar">نِقْضٌ</foreign> in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">مَنْقُوضٌ</foreign>: (TA:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">طُرُوفٌ</foreign> (As, S, O, K) and <foreign lang="ar">أَطْرَافٌ</foreign>: (O, K:) accord. to AZ, an epithet applied peculiarly to the <hi rend="ital">males:</hi> (S, O, K: *) or <hi rend="ital">generous in respect of the sires and the dams:</hi> (Lth, O, K:) or <hi rend="ital">recently acquired; not of his owner's breeding;</hi> fem. with <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign>, (O, K,) occurring in a verse of El-'Ajjáj: Lth says that they sometimes apply the epithets <foreign lang="ar">طِرْفٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">طِرْفَةٌ</foreign> as syn. with <foreign lang="ar">نَجِيبٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">نَجِيبَةٌ</foreign>, in a manner unusual in the language: (O:) accord. to Ks, <foreign lang="ar">طِرْفَةٌ</foreign> is applied as an epithet to a mare: (TA:) and <foreign lang="ar">طِرْفٌ</foreign> signifies also a horse <hi rend="ital">long in the legs</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the neck, having the ears pointed, tapering,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">slender at the extremities.</hi> (TA in the supplement to this art.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  And <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">Generous</hi> (S, O, TA) as an epithet applied to a young man (S, TA) or to a man; (O, TA;) as also

                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">طَرَفٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> The <hi rend="ital">extremity,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">end,</hi> of anything; [as of a sword, and of a spear, and of a rope, and of the tongue, &amp;c.;] thus accord. to ISd; but in the K this meaning is assigned to   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n26616-1" target="طَرْفٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n26613"/></foreign>: (TA: [several evidences of the correctness of the former word in this sense will be found in the present art.; and countless instances of it occur in other arts. &amp;c.: it seems to have been generally regarded by the lexicographers as too notorious to need its being mentioned:]) and <hi rend="ital">a side; a lateral,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an outward,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">adjacent, part</hi> or <hi rend="ital">portion; a region, district, quarter,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">tract;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">نَاحِيَةٌ</foreign>: (S, O, Msb, K:) and <hi rend="ital">a part, portion, piece,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">bit,</hi> (syn. <foreign lang="ar">طَائِفَةٌ</foreign>,) of a thing: (S, O, K:) it is used in relation to bodies, or material things, and to times &amp;c.; (Er-Rághib, TA;) and is thus used in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">طَائِفَة</foreign> of a people, in the Kur iii. 122; (Ksh;) [and may often be rendered <hi rend="ital">somewhat</hi> of a thing, whether material (as land &amp;c.) or not material (as in the T and S voce <foreign lang="ar">ذَرْوٌ</foreign>, where it is used of a saying, and as in the S and A and K in art. <foreign lang="ar">هوس</foreign> &amp;c., where it is used of madness, or insanity, or diabolical possession):] the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">أَطْرَافٌ</foreign>. (O, Msb, K.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">الأَطْرَافُ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">The fingers:</hi> and [when relating to the fingers] has no sing. unless this is used as a prefixed noun, as in the saying <foreign lang="ar">أَشَارَتْ بِطَرَفِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">إِصْبَعِهَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">She made a sign with the end of her finger</hi>]: but the pl. is said by Az to be used in the sense of the sing. in the following ex. cited by Fr, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">يُبْدِينَ أَطْرَافًا لِطَافًا عَنَيَهٌ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [so that the meaning is, <hi rend="ital">They show an elegant finger</hi> like <hi rend="ital">a fruit of the species of tree called</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَنَم</foreign>]; therefore the poet says <foreign lang="ar">عَمَنَه</foreign> [which is a n. un.: but I think that it is much more reasonable, and especially as the verb is pl., to regard the <foreign lang="ar">ه</foreign> in this case as the <foreign lang="ar">ه</foreign> of pausation, of which see an ex. voce <foreign lang="ar">حِينٌ</foreign>; and accordingly to render the saying, <hi rend="ital">they show elegant fingers</hi> like <hi rend="ital">fruits of the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَنَم</foreign>]. (TA.) It is said in a trad. of Abraham, when he was a little child, <foreign lang="ar">جُعِلَ رِزْقُهُ</foreign>
